    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_360022117" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/360022117" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4075354-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606221712p2/4075354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/360022117?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/4075354-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17158481-the-fairest-beauty">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=re-tellings">re-tellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=cfd-bookclub">cfd-bookclub</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer360022117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18163248972594435894">I love fairy tale re-tellings. There is just something about knowing the old story, yet reading it in a fresh new style. Dickerson definitely delivers that with The Fairest Beauty. Having read her first two books, I have to say that I enjoyed this one the most. The plot was more fast moving and more adventuresome than how I remember the first two. There were definitely big things at stake, which lent a more urgency to the story.<br/><br/>What keeps from bumping it up to five stars is that some of the char</span>
  <span id="freeText18163248972594435894" style="display:none">I love fairy tale re-tellings. There is just something about knowing the old story, yet reading it in a fresh new style. Dickerson definitely delivers that with The Fairest Beauty. Having read her first two books, I have to say that I enjoyed this one the most. The plot was more fast moving and more adventuresome than how I remember the first two. There were definitely big things at stake, which lent a more urgency to the story.<br /><br />What keeps from bumping it up to five stars is that some of the characters just didn't have enough depth for me. Sophie is nearly perfect - she's beautiful, always kindhearted (even in her thoughts toward the evil duchess who is trying to kill her!) and just wasn't someone I could always relate with. Some of her decisions were way too naive - I wanted more of a twist with the "old woman" and apple scenario. It was very Disney-esque. Now, for the fairy tale aspect, I suppose that it makes sense that she is kind and perfect and good, but at times it was a bit much. I liked Gabe much more! He was endearing, impulsive, foolhardy, stubborn and all-around likable - there were real flaws there and that made him realistic in a way that Sophie never becomes for me.<br /><br />There are also a couple of plot points that come across as devices instead of naturally occurring in the story, and the ending was very "deus ex machina." Something just happens to make everything easier on the characters, and I thought it just came across as too convenient.<br /><br />Despite these two issues, I still had fun reading this story. I loved the "Seven," and the way she twists the seven dwarfs idea around a bit with their different characteristics. They weren't cookie-cutter with the different characteristics, which I really loved. The romance is also really sweet, and I thought it was very well-done. While it might have been shorter compared to other stories, it fit in well with the fairy tale element.<br /><br />I found the family aspect of the story to be well-done too. Gabe &amp; Sophie have to realize that their actions have consequences not only for them but also for their family, and the way they rise to occasion when this happens is admirable. They draw strength from their faith without the spiritual elements coming across as preachy. It felt very natural within the story.<br /><br />It was also neat to see the characters from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7826101.The_Healer_s_Apprentice__Fairy_Tales__1_" title="The Healer's Apprentice (Fairy Tales #1) by Melanie Dickerson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Healer's Apprentice</a> at the end of the story - it was a very subtle connection, but fun if you've read the first book. I don't think it would be a problem to read this one first though as no plot-points of the previous book are given away.<br /><br /> I realize that I'm not technically the intended audience for this book - I'd imagine a young teen girl probably would have no problem with the things in which I found issue. Even so, I loved this for being a light, fun fairy tale with characters that had many admirable, endearing qualities.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18163248972594435894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1616930145" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1616930145" />
    <a title="E.F.B." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39244832-e-f-b"><img alt="E.F.B." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424876183p2/39244832.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1616930145?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="E.F.B." class="user" itemprop="url" name="E.F.B." href="/user/show/39244832-e-f-b">E.F.B.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to E.F.B. by: </span>
      a Goodreads friend
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=books-i-ll-read-again">books-i-ll-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=fairy-tale-retellings">fairy-tale-retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=made-me-smile">made-me-smile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1616930145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2811999037381062325">Solid 4 stars<br/><br/>Another hit from Melanie Dickerson! I know I’ve said it before, but I will say it again: I love her books. <3 “The Fairest Beauty” was a retelling of the fairytale, “Snow White” but without magic because it is in a historical setting. <br/><br/>There are only a few small reasons I’m giving this one 4 instead of 5 stars. First, I’ve been feeling like I give 5 star ratings out a little too easily lately, and second, there are actual story things (but only very, very, small things) that I could </span>
  <span id="freeText2811999037381062325" style="display:none">Solid 4 stars<br><br>Another hit from Melanie Dickerson! I know I’ve said it before, but I will say it again: I love her books. &lt;3 “The Fairest Beauty” was a retelling of the fairytale, “Snow White” but without magic because it is in a historical setting. <br><br>There are only a few small reasons I’m giving this one 4 instead of 5 stars. First, I’ve been feeling like I give 5 star ratings out a little too easily lately, and second, there are actual story things (but only very, very, small things) that I could mention that I either didn’t like or took away from the story just a little bit.<br><br>In the other three Melanie Dickerson books I’ve read, I’ve been 100% behind the male protagonists from page one. I didn’t question their motives or whether or not he was the best person for the heroine, but that wasn’t necessarily the case here. I’m not saying I wasn’t behind the male protagonist AT ALL: Gabe was very nice and likable and I was behind him at least 85%-90% through the majority of the story. Buuuut… in the other books of Melanie’s that I’ve read, the male protagonist is usually the steady, mature, responsible one. Gabe, however, was the opposite. At the start of the story he was flighty, and a tad immature and irresponsible, especially in comparison to his brother, Valten, to whom Sophie was supposed to be betrothed. I found myself wondering if he was truly in love with Sophie and wanted the best for her, or if he was just infatuated with her, *thought* he wanted the best for her, but was really just wanting to prove himself and one-up his brother. However, Gabe himself ended up acknowledging and grappling with these things too, and by the time he worked them out, I was able to finally get 100% behind him.<br><br>Also, I couldn’t help feeling a little bad for Gabe’s brother, Valten, while being miffed with him at the same time. I mean, on one hand it’s not like he meant to break his leg right before they found out about Sophie and how she needed help, and I can understand not wanting your younger brother to rescue your betrothed for you. <br><br>But on the other hand…Dude, the old woman said the girl was in DANGER and both you AND your father want to wait until your leg is healed and his obligations are cleared to take the TWO WEEK JOURNEY to go out there and see if she really is the person the old woman said she is and if she really is in danger rather than just send your younger brother out there in your place??? DUDE! I THOUGHT YOU AND ESPECIALLY WILHELM WERE SMARTER THAN THAT!!! Dudes.<br><br>On the Other other hand, when we got in Valten’s head after his leg healed and he met Sophie, I felt sorry for him again because it seemed like he really did just want to find Sophie and protect her and be a good (future) husband, but it turns out that physically speaking, he’s huge and intimidating and has some scars on his face and so women tend to be afraid of him even though he doesn’t mean to be scary.<br><br>On the OTHER Other other hand, he might be less scary if he…you know…actually SMILED every once in a while. Seriously dude, it’s not going to break your face, and you could work on your conversational skills as well. Ultimately, I felt like he was definitely not the right person for sweet little friendly Sophie. But, especially based on the way his sisters seemed to adore him and he seemed to adore them in his own quiet understated way, I don’t think he’s a bad guy, and now I’m hoping that one of the later books might involve him finding a true love of his own. <br><br>Now I’ll talk about Duchess Ermengard. If you’ve read the story, I doubt I have to say much more, but for those who haven’t read it, the Duchess was… How shall I describe her? She was…she was…<br><br><a href="http://s1287.photobucket.com/user/craftyelfringer/media/Randomness/addtext_com_MTExMDQ5MzE5MjE.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487965892i/22069285._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo addtext_com_MTExMDQ5MzE5MjE.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Ah, yes, thank you old guy from The Emperor’s New Groove. She was SCARY BEYOND ALL REASON!!! And here I thought the bad guy from “The Healer’s Apprentice” was creepy, but Duchess Ermengard “takes the cake” so to speak. Not that I think Duchess Ermengard would actually eat cake. She’d much rather use the icing as makeup to cover the wrinkles on her creepy, haggard face. Seems evil is bad for one’s complexion…<br><br>In all seriousness, though, Duchess Ermengard was truly creepy and evil as everything. This was made even worse because we get several chapters/scenes written from her perspective and, oh my goodness, was that woman ever insane! She is much like the evil queen from the Snow White story because she hates Sophie simply because Sophie is prettier than her, and nicer than her, and overall a better, more likable person. Therefore, she is absolutely horrid to Sophie (and anyone else who crosses her) by verbally and physically abusing her, treats her like a slave, and eventually tries to kill her. I just really didn’t like the parts where we were in her head because of her evilness, and occasionally, she was a little gross too. Also, I didn’t understand, and it was never explained why the Duke married Ermengard in the first place. I mean, I kind of assumed that maybe, with the grief over the death of his first wife he wasn’t thinking straight and maybe Ermengard deceived him because she wanted his money or whatever, but like I said, it was actually never explained that I recall.<br><br>I also felt that the part where Sophie and Gabe were traveling from Hohendorf to the Cottage of the Seven was a teeny bit longer than it needed to be and by the time they got to the cottage I was ready for the story to move forward.<br><br>BUT! Overall, this book was enjoyable. and it was so sweet, and so romantic, and I especially appreciate how Melanie is so good and slipping in Christian themes without being preachy or heavy handed, but it’s still impactful. I especially like how her female protagonists are so hungry for learning, and how her male protagonists truly respect women and honor them and protect them. AND the men being protective of the women doesn’t mean that the women are helpless or lesser in any way. Sophie, while being young, and innocent, and living in a society where women didn’t have all the opportunities and rights of men, was not stupid, she was not helpless, and she was not weak. She ended up being my favorite character in the book, which is interesting because when it first started out, I was afraid she sounded too “practically perfect in every way”. But when we got to know her, she did have fears and flaws and things she had to overcome, and I related to her a lot, though our situations in life are very different.<br><br> I would recommend this to lovers of historical fiction, fairytale retellings, and sweet, clean romance 15 years old and up.<br><br>Content stuff for those who want to know: There is some mild violence and some peril in this book. People get wounds that are bloody and may be potentially life-threatening, but none of it is described in a way that I personally found icky or disturbing. One person drowns. As I mentioned in my review, the Duchess is evil, insane, and occasionally disgusting. Evil and insane because she treats everyone horribly even when they haven’t done anything to her besides existing and we become aware that she kills and/or mentally tortures people she doesn’t like, or who become useless to her, or who are more beautiful than her, and she is obsessed over these things. Disgusting because, when she decided she wanted Sophie killed, she wanted the huntsman to cut Sophie’s heart out and bring it to her. As she debated what to do with the heart when she got it, we heard how she she thought about drying it and putting it on display like a trophy or even eating it because she heard that there are some cultures where they eat the hearts of their enemies to gain strength. *shudder*<br><br>“On-screen” sexual stuff is limited to kissing and overall obvious physical attraction between the protagonists, though there are extremely vague allusions made to things like a servant girl boasting that she had a “very good time” while staying out all night with the huntsman, Gabe wanting to find someone to travel with him and Sophie as soon as possible because it’s not going to be good for Sophie’s or his reputation if people find out they were traveling alone together for so long even though, of course, they didn't do anything inappropriate, etc. (Reviewer note: I LOVED the way Sophie handled that servant girl’s boasts! Go Sophie! XD) These things are the reason I said I would recommend this for readers 15 and up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2811999037381062325" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1098877510" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1098877510" />
    <a title="Nastassja Loots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18733657-nastassja-loots"><img alt="Nastassja Loots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364279612p2/18733657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1098877510?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nastassja Loots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nastassja Loots" href="/user/show/18733657-nastassja-loots">Nastassja Loots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1098877510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13479903312139346583">I hate giving bad reviews. Truly, I take no pleasure in criticizing someone else's efforts - However, I am always truthful in my reviews, and I have to start of by saying this book took me forever to read. It did not hold my attention, I never became emotionally invested in the outcome and I had to force myself to finish it. I'm still in the process of trying to retrain my brain to abandon books I don't enjoy, but alas, I still have mild OCD when it comes to finishing what I start.<br/><br/>From the blurb</span>
  <span id="freeText13479903312139346583" style="display:none">I hate giving bad reviews. Truly, I take no pleasure in criticizing someone else's efforts - However, I am always truthful in my reviews, and I have to start of by saying this book took me forever to read. It did not hold my attention, I never became emotionally invested in the outcome and I had to force myself to finish it. I'm still in the process of trying to retrain my brain to abandon books I don't enjoy, but alas, I still have mild OCD when it comes to finishing what I start.<br /><br />From the blurb I assume it is understood that this is a retelling of Snow White. While I usually enjoy a fresh take on a classic, I just did not enjoy this book at all. This isn't going to be a detailed review, I will just point out what I have a problem with. First of all, I don't like the characters. Sophie is just way too good to be true. She is portrayed as this perfect person who memorizes and quotes Scripture, and never sins. Ever. She doesn't even harbour ill feelings towards her stepmother who abuses everyone around her. This is just absolutely unrealistic and makes it impossible to relate to Sophie. As for Gabe, he is portrayed as arrogant and self-indulgent - kind of hard to like a "hero" when the only reason he went to rescue Sophie was to stick it to his brother. Against his parents' direct instructions and against Valten's wishes, Gabe nevertheless went to find Sophie by himself. It is expressly stated in the book several times how much joy Gabe gets from being the one to find his brother's fiancee. Later he tries to convince himself and everyone around him that God placed the desire in his heart and that it must have been God's will for him to be the one to find Sophie. I have a HUGE problem with this approach considering this book is classified as religious fiction. Please remember, Ms Dickerson, that honour thy father and mother is one of the ten commandments. You can't have your character wilfully disobey his parents for purely selfish reasons and try to justify it by claiming that it was God's will. This can be very confusing for non-believers reading this book as it is a pretty big contradiction. I would rather have had Gabe not try to justify his behaviour at all, admit he did something wrong and learn from it - that would have been more realistic, as well. <br /><br />Ermengard (another problem I have is the author using annoying, hard to pronounce names) is a ridiculous villain and I couldn't take her seriously. She's so pathetic, I questioned the backbone and integrity of the whole cast of characters who allowed her to treat them the way they did. I also had no respect for Sophie's father who deserted his Kingdom after Ermengard tricked him into believing Sophie had died. He just up and left, leaving his loyal subjects to be tormented by his evil wife. <br /><br />Last, but not least, I did not see any chemistry between Sophie and Gabe. Their relationship was not believable to me and I had no emotional connection to either of them. I had developed more feelings towards Valten in the limited time I got to spend with him (ten pages?) than I ever had for either Sophie or Gabe.<br /><br />Towards the end of the book I just started skipping sections, wanting to reach the end; I even skimmed right over the final confrontation between Sophie and Ermengard (which should have been gripping, right?). Sadly I just did not enjoy this book at all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13479903312139346583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_497788517" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/497788517" />
    <a title="Erin " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2997696-erin"><img alt="Erin " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531863934p2/2997696.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/497788517?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin " href="/user/show/2997696-erin">Erin </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer497788517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11346700307772292028">Melanie Dickerson has done it again, offering readers another imaginative fairy tale adaptation, this time taking on the classic Snow White in her third release, The Fairest Beauty. <br/><br/>As with her first two books, Dickerson combines the classic tale with both history and religion. While I've seen fairy tales mixed with history before, Dickerson is the only author I've encountered to have infused the classic stories with faith. It is an interesting combination to say the least, one that creates a ra</span>
  <span id="freeText11346700307772292028" style="display:none">Melanie Dickerson has done it again, offering readers another imaginative fairy tale adaptation, this time taking on the classic Snow White in her third release, The Fairest Beauty. <br /><br />As with her first two books, Dickerson combines the classic tale with both history and religion. While I've seen fairy tales mixed with history before, Dickerson is the only author I've encountered to have infused the classic stories with faith. It is an interesting combination to say the least, one that creates a rather original twist. <br /><br />I personal don't mind inspired literature and don't consider the use of religious themes a factor when rating the books I read, but I will say I felt the theological material in The Fairest Beauty is featured more prominently than it was in The Healer's Apprentice or The Merchant's Daughter. Might be something to think about if you are the kind of reader who doesn't appreciate faith based lit. <br /><br />I did like some of the other twists Dickerson offered, the concept she used for The Seven in particular, but like many other reviewers feel there were a lot on plot twists that seemed simply too convenient and made things too easy on Gabe and Sophie. Call me crazy, but I like when the odds are a little less in the protagonist's favor. <br /><br />That aside my only real disappointment came in the form of Duchess Ermengard. I'm sorry, but the inherently wicked stepmother doesn't appeal to me. Yes, I am bias because I am a member of the E.V.I.L. sisterhood, but even so, I find it disheartening that even in re-imagined adaptations the stepmother role enjoys little if any metamorphosis. I realize there needs to be a bad guy, but that being said we've given strength to the traditionally vulnerable role of Snow White, can we try giving some depth to the queen, some real motivation for her hatred and anger? <br /><br />Despite feeling that Dickerson didn't offer up any truly ground-breaking variation to the story, I feel the book is pleasantly distinctive and will appeal to those looking for lighter reading material. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11346700307772292028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Rosie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8198729-rosie"><img alt="Rosie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520196058p2/8198729.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/376086980?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosie" href="/user/show/8198729-rosie">Rosie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8198729-rosie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer376086980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3784800076769396084">Another enchanting read from Melanie Dickerson!<br/><br/>The Fairest Beauty revolves around Gabe, son of Rose and Wilhelm (their story was told in The Healer's Apprentice), and Sophie, daughter of Duke Baldwin and betrothed to Gabe's older brother, Valten. Having only read The Healer's Apprentice previously by Melanie, it excited me to know that I'd learn more about Rose and Wilhelm and their family.<br/><br/>This retelling of the story of Snow White (who seems to be quite popular this year!), is fabulously done. I</span>
  <span id="freeText3784800076769396084" style="display:none">Another enchanting read from Melanie Dickerson!<br /><br />The Fairest Beauty revolves around Gabe, son of Rose and Wilhelm (their story was told in The Healer's Apprentice), and Sophie, daughter of Duke Baldwin and betrothed to Gabe's older brother, Valten. Having only read The Healer's Apprentice previously by Melanie, it excited me to know that I'd learn more about Rose and Wilhelm and their family.<br /><br />This retelling of the story of Snow White (who seems to be quite popular this year!), is fabulously done. It incorporates twists I could have never anticipated and brings the story to life, especially after a year of Snow White movies and shows. I am quite impressed with The Fairest Beauty. The writing and characters meet expectations and the story will pull you in until the last page.<br /><br />As always, the underlying Christian message slid in like a puzzle piece with Sophie's troubles as well as Gabe's. I really hurt for Sophie as she tried to heal from all of the hurtful lies the evil Duchess spewed at her over the years. It certainly isn't something that occurs overnight! While, Gabe's problems might seem trivial compared to Sophie's they are real. I won't say too much more, I'd hate to spoil a great book like this one!<br /><br />In conclusion, I really, really, liked Melanie's latest! I'm crossing my fingers as to which fairytale she'll do next! And I secretly hope it will involve Valten. :-) <br /><br />I received this book from DJC Communications in return for an honest review of my opinions, which I have done. Thanks!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer600559821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12291968321932853611">I loved it. And YA is not usually my favorite genre, but this was so romantic yet so clean. I loved Sophie. She was the perfect heroine. And Gabe grew so much. Now I need to find more books by this author. Why have I never read anything by her before?!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nfbirnm/IOfFNGcWGsoKnxHkGW8Af22XXmt1QdAgAnDtrmEiWtxR1xDCR5JLD2nHOkSp9dxT0BfL4BtYLzu8vQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GdWbodxSmp+g9GAQch7YPvW5lgKrViPxHZBxkreO6XNpjRgt/zHrr3UCQJQj27tm3hkmmHd6nnGIGx+LSJVXvg==')})
  }
//]]>

Lord Collin remembers Juliana from their childhood—and challenges her to stay on his estate for a week in hopes she will leave her thieving ways and become a proper lady once more. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer359279704825212288">Melanie Dickerson is a New York Times bestselling author, a two-time Christy Award finalist, two-time Maggie Award winner, Carol Award winner, two-time winner of the Christian Retailing's Best award, and her book, The Healer's Apprentice, won the National Readers Choice Award for Best First Book. She is a member of American Christian Fiction Writers (ACFW) and Romance Writers of America (RWA). Mel</span>
  <span id="freeText359279704825212288" style="display:none">Melanie Dickerson is a New York Times bestselling author, a two-time Christy Award finalist, two-time Maggie Award winner, Carol Award winner, two-time winner of the Christian Retailing's Best award, and her book, The Healer's Apprentice, won the National Readers Choice Award for Best First Book. She is a member of American Christian Fiction Writers (ACFW) and Romance Writers of America (RWA). Melanie earned a bachelors degree in special education of the hearing impaired from The University of Alabama and has worked as a teacher in Georgia, Tennessee, and Ukraine. She lives with her husband and two children in Huntsville, Alabama.</span>
